<Author>ALLOVERPOINTS
<Content>Perfect Location! This hotel was fantastic. I was a little concerned by some of the other reviews before booking, considering we were using a very large amount of points to stay for New Year's. We arrived on Tues. Dec. 30, to wonderful and quick check in, and an upgraded room that overlooked Times Square that we requested upon booking. We were not disappointed. Yes, the hotel is quite large, and the lift system could be intimidating, but actually very easy. This was most likely the busiest time being New Year's and we had no trouble whatsoever with waiting for elevators. Even after the ball dropped it only took 15-20 min. to get back into our room. The hotel itself is in the best location. It is within walking distance to everything, and we walked, and walked, and walked until we saw it all. I would not recommend taking kids on a New York City trip, but if you did, you would find plenty for them to do near this hotel. The giant Toysrus across the street alone would provide hours of entertainment with the giant ferris wheel and walk in barbie house. You can be at Rockefeller center in minutes and we even braved the Subway which was way easier than I ever anticipated. Overall the location could not be beat, and the service was excellent. We were comped free breakfast in the hotel restaurant every morning ($70 every day) and the staff were above and beyond helpful with directions, mapping out every detail for us to get from point a to b, and making reservations at whatever our request was. The hotel was very clean, and housekeeping was great adhering to our schedule each day. Had a great and exhausting time trying to see it all. Thank goodness our home base was Times Square. Oh and the best part is you are directly across from ABC studio where they tape Good Morning America, so you can get up and walk across the street and see yourself on TV. Too funny. Enjoy!

So - we opted for a king room that was available immediately that overlooked Broadway. This room was great! We had the last room at the end of the hall (3224) king bed and a little sitting area with a sofa bed. Very roomy! The bath was small and it was a little tough for both of us to get ready there at the same time.The room look like it had been updated somewhat recently - at least with the furnishings, carpet and the bedding - but it was tired in a few areas. There was a large flat-panel TV that we never turned on and a desk and chair if you're doing a little work as well. I think they charge $17/day for the internet - which I think is a bit excessive - but that's just my opinion.The window was on the small side too, but we looked directly out at the Virgin store and just to the right is 1 Times Square where they drop the ball on New Year's Eve. Needless to say, we were happy with the room and stayed even after the front desk called to say they had a Times Square view become available.I suppose I should back up the bus a bit and say this hotel is HUGE! Something like 2000 rooms and you can tell that by going to the elevator bank where there are 15 elevators! Crazy! We never really waited all that long, but there were a couple of occasions where we were jammed into a elevator with too many people - I'm sure we looked like circus clowns getting out of a VW a few times...Anyway, the lobby is on the 8th floor and that's where you'll find a Starbucks, shopping and a restaurant and bar. There is the View bar at the top (or close?) of the hotel and it moves....ever so slowly...but there was a line of probably 30 people waiting and it seemed to be a big hit. We had a few nice drinks but didn't eat so I can't comment on the food. There is also another Starbuck's on the first floor as well.The first floor let's you out in every direction, so it's nice you don't have to walk around an entire block to go in/out. Everything and anything you can think of that you want to see is in walking distance (this IS New York - so bring your comfortable walking shoes!!!!!!) The Lion King theatre is across the street, as is the one that Katie Holmes is starring in now. There were tons of people hoping for a Mr. and Mrs. Cruise sighting - so be prepared for larger than average crowds in front of this theatre!If you go out the Broadway door, maybe you'll get to see the Naked Cowboy! This is where he hangs out (ew!) and there is always quite a crowd around him as well.A quick tip....We had purchased a New York Pass and did the hop on/hop off CitySights open top bus tour - which is a bit corny but it was really nice. We also did the Circle Line cruise to the Statue of Liberty - that was very cool. If you intend on spending a few days going to several sights, I do recommend buying a pass. Our three-day pass got us into several museums, the bus rides, the cruise and the Empire State building - all included in one price. It was very handy.Back to the hotel....They did a great job with Wine Specator event - we were amazed at how quickly they transformed the ballroom spaces. The staff was professional and friendly and it didn't seem like we were just another event - so kudos to everyone.Some people have mentioned how busy the hotel is or how busy the streets are by the hotel. Um, this is TIMES SQUARE! If you want a peaceful, boutique-y stay....go to Tribeca. If you want to walk out your door and be in the thick of things....the Marquis is a great base camp for what I'm sure will be a great New York experience!Happy Travels!LisaMinneapolis

Be careful as they try to pull the trick of putting an AUTOMATIC 18%!!!!!!! surcharge on the bill if u have more than 4 people. We had 5, so the $500 bill for the trash we ate went up t0 590. Rediculous! Moving on. Being a large hotel, service was lacking slightly, and it took a long time to get anything. Putting that aside, it was a top quality Marriott. The room I stayed in was newly furnished, with new TV and had a fantastic view over times square. Saying that, LOCATION LOCATION BABY!!!! This hotel is fantastc. Right in the middle of everything, walk out the door and Times Square just hits you. A great place. So, to wrap it up. A busy hotel, but to expected in Times Square, bad food in typical marriott fashion, but a irreplacable location and a great room. It definately was an experience I will never forget.

<Author>ks3804
<Content>A great first NYC experience We stayed here over a long weekend in early April '08. Check in was fast and stress-free (there was a line when we arrived but it moved quickly) and the staff was very welcoming. Our room was ready right away (well before the official check in time), and was clean and spacious, very little to argue with there. There's several food options there if you feel like staying in at any point on your trip -- we ate at the restaurant on the top floor (which was decent but expensive), as well as one of the restaurants on a lower floor for breakfast and the lounge for drinks (again, both were good and the revolving lounge is fun, but both, like many places in NYC, are a little pricey.) The location is a huge selling point for this place and for first-timers in NYC like we were it was a good place to be based (you have Times Square obviously right outside your door, and we were able to easily walk to a lot of sights like the Museum of Modern Art -- but keep in mind that we are both healthy young adults with no children so your mileage may vary.) Getting to the subway from the hotel was also easy. The only thing I can't really comment on is the price of the room, since we were able to stay mostly on Marriott rewards program points and therefore got a really good deal. All in all, I would book this place with confidence and recommend it to others.

<Author>Samee-Judge
<Content>Big, Great Location, Service Okay, $$$$$ This is a good hotel for business, or a quick trip to NYC. It's not a resort, other than the fitness center (which is great), there is not much to do in the hotel. This hotel is big, and the elevators can be slow. I did have one problem with the an electrical outlet in the room. I called and reported it in the morning, but it was not fixed when I returned in the evening. Other than that everything in the room worked well. The toilets are loud, and you can here others flush.The fitness center is great. A lot of equipment. The club lounge on the 30th floor is big, and a nice assortment of food and beverages available for reward members or those willing to pay for the access. I had breakfast in their coffee shop one morning at it cost about $100.00 for four persons. It is NYC. The staff is friendly, but the hotel is so big, you don't get the high touch service you might find at other Marriott's. Oh, and carry a lot of dollar bills with you because everytime someone does something for you they expect a tip. It is NYC. One last thing. Although, check-in and getting through security at LGA took 15min at the Delta Terminal. Not sure if that's normal, or I just hit it at the right time.

<Author>Fenway7
<Content>Great central NYC location! There's no better place to stay if you want to be right in the middle of it all! Smack in the middle of the wonderful chaos that is Times Square, mere feet away from the best of Broadway (including the half-price ticket line), and subway stations. Walking distance to Rockefeller center, Central Park, and other top NYC destinations! Of course this location means sirens and honking taxicabs at all hours, as well as hoards of pedestrians and tourists filling every inch of the sidewalk. Don't stay here if you're looking for peace and quiet, although I must say the windows are fairly successful at keeping out all the noise. The rotating restaurant on the roof is a must-see, even if just for drinks. It's too bad they took out the rotating cafe on the main lobby floor, but the new renovations and additional restaurants are wonderful! Weekend brunch is a pretty good value too, especially since the restaurants right outside your door are incredibly overpriced. Get out of Times Square if you're looking for a more authentic NYC experience. The Marriott Marquis can't be beat though if you want to stay right in Times Square/Broadway!! I've stayed here many times, with family and for business, and I keep coming back.

<Content>Marriott Marquis Times Square -Great Location for Tourists I spent 2 nights this past week at the Marquis. I was in NYC for a training and spent a Wednesday  Thursday night. I got a government rate due to my job so my rate was significantly cheaper than the going rate and I booked directly through Marriott.com.I took Amtrak in to Penn Station and I am pretty comfortable traveling around NYC so I took the subway, 1 stop to Times Square and then a couple block walk to the hotel. The check-in desk in on the 8th floor which was a bit odd, but no big deal. Check-in was far and away the worst part of the whole stay. 3 clerks were working when I arrived, each was busy. A line formed behind me as we waited for our turn. 2 of the 3 clerks were dealing with different problems with the guests. The 3rd clerk finally finished with their guest and told us to wait for someone else, and he walked away. That was really annoying. I proceeded to wait a total of 15 minutes before I was checked in. Too long to wait at 8pm at night after traveling and with luggage. (Frankly, too long to wait any time of the day!) The clerk who checked me in did not impress me with his customer service, but I wouldn't call him rude.My room was on the 39th floor, 2 Queen Sized beds. The elevator was a little slow for me since I was on one of the top floors. Someone has to stay on those floors, though-right? My room was impecably clean. The bath products were Bath  Body Works. There were 4 fluffy towels in my room. There was also a coffee maker which I didn't use.Large flat screen LCD TV was great, got most channels I wanted except no Food Network or Comedy Central. Oh well, not there to watch TV but they are basic cable channels so I was disappointed. The view was of Times Square and I didn't even shut the black out curtains at night. The view was great and the lights did not bother me at all.The bed was comfortable, the pillows were a little bit mushy for my taste, but workable. There was an i-Pod docking station/alarm clock which I thought was a nice touch.The internet was WIRED and cost $16.95/day-at least it should have been wireless at that price! What a rip-off. And it goes noon to noon not 24 hours from when you purchase. I was NOT impressed with that. I like to sit on my bed and do work when I travel as many others do, but that wasn't possible with wired access. I was able to pull it close enough to put my feet up on a bed but that was it. The connection speed was mediocre at best. Again for the price it should have been much better. So that was a little disappointing.The AC was fine, I like the room pretty cool so it was hard for me to tell if the AC wasn't working well or it was me. The room was around 67 the whole time, I would have preferred 65.With my TV on I couldn't hear anyone else in surrounding rooms. There is a Starbucks on the 8th and 1st floors of this hotel as well as numerous restaurants. For $10 I was able to eat a decent Starbucks breakfast each day of my stay as compared to the hotel restaraunt buffet at $28pp plus tax and gratuity. (Welcome to New York my friends!) The cheapest thing on the a la carte breakfast menu was a $10 fruit cup! So Starbucks it is! The room service menu was as expensive as can be expected, but you are in NYC, in an expensive hotel and in the middle of Times Square. There is however a shop on the 8th floor of the hotel, honestly the prices were much more reasonable than I expected in the shop. Snacks, soft drinks and gift items. You can eat for less money in this area, but you really have to look for it. There is a deli on the corner of 49th/Broadway with great sandwiches-$10 for lunch...So all in all the room was clean, I slept well. I don't think I would have stayed here at the $400+ a night rate, but for $210 a night it was fine. Very upscale for foreign tourists and high-end business class. With my little ol' government rate I didn't quite fit here, but that was ok. Very convenient to where I needed to be.

<Author>alibeth
<Content>Definetly a hotel for tourists in the big apple! We booked this hotel after leaving the Jumeirah Essex hotel wanting to stay 1/2 of the time near Central Park and 1/2 near Times Square. Also you have the ticket booth for broadway shows right outside your door for 50% off or the regular tickets right in the hotel. Starbucks is in the hotel which, believe me, is an easier way of getting coffee than finding a place in Times Square. Kevin and Robert, who checked us in, did everything to get us a connecting room since we had two rooms. Great Job! We got a rate that included breakfast, plus pancakes and waffles. Good buffet. You'll leave here not knowing how they run the place with all those people. Concierge polite and gave us directions every time we wanted to go somewhere. You push which floor you want and then it tells you alphabetically which elevator to get on. Time Square is really busy if you like crowds and the Marriott Marquis is in the middle of it. If you're looking for great pizza, John's pizza is only a block away and one of the best in NY.

<Author>Stella20
<Content>Magic at the Marquis I have just returned from a 5 night stay at the Marriott Marquis with my family which includes fifty somethings and 18-21 year olds and would thoroughly recommend it as the perfect place to stay for the first time visitor to New York. We all loved the location, comfort and sheer luxury of this hotel. The location, right in the middle of the Times Square area, was ideal for walking to the nearer must-see tourist attractions, such as the Empire State Building, Grand Central Station, Macy's, the Rockefeller Centre, Central Park and Broadway shows. It was also a dropping off point for the open-toppped tour buses when you want to go further afield. We made full use of a 2 day pass on the Grayline buses to explore Chinatown, Little Italy, Greenwich Village, Harlem, Brooklyn and the Seaport district. One of the highlights of our visit was the night tour - the view of the Manhattan skyline and the bridges at dusk was sheer magic! The hotel also impressed us with the clean, comfortable and spacious rooms and the helpfulness of all the staff we encountered. From the people on the ground floor who arranged the luggage and taxis to the courteous receptionist who organised 3 rooms close together with good views to the chambermaids and waitresses who looked after our needs after exhausting days sightseeing everyone was polite and friendly (and we found the tipping system easy to manage, no-one seemed to expect huge amounts).The elevator system worked well for us, we never waited more than about 30 seconds even on peak times and the views were great.One point - I have seen many tourists asking about taxis and airport transport - we were a party of 5 adults and had no problems in getting a yellow cab to and from JFK at a set rate of 45 dollars + toll and tip. The hotel organised this when we left and also stored our bags for the day as we had an evening flight.We enjoyed a visit to the View restaurant at the top of the hotel - about 8-9 is best to get a full revolution and see the lights come on and the sunset over NY. This, plus walking the Brooklyn Bridge and the night bus tour were our favourite memories of our trip - New York at all levels! We would all love to return, preferably in December to see the city in a different season and would definitely stay at the Marquis again. Hope this review is helpful and enjoy your holiday as much as we did!

<Author>MFLetou
<Content>A pleasant stay in the heart of Times Square We stayed at the New York Marriott Marquis for three nights over a recent (busy) weekend in New York (in fact, the hotel was sold out one of the nights, no small feat for such a huge facility). We had also considered the Renaissance Times Square, but ended up pleased with our choice.First of all, the hotel is literally in the middle of Times Square, which has its pluses and minuses. On the positive side, nothing can beat the scene--or the view from many of the rooms--of the flashing neon and people. Times Square is an excellent location for tourists because its the middle of the city, with easy access to most subway lines that can take you downtown or uptown. A cab ride to Greenwich Village was about 10-12 minutes.On the negative side, the rush of the crowd right outside the doors does get to be a bit overwhelming and annoying--you've really got to fight your way just to get back to the hotel, even late at night. But for the purposes of our trip, which was a nice getaway (without the kid) for the weekend, it served us well.The hotel itself is rather stunning inside due to the large atrium. Considering the size of the place, most things are efficient--the high tech elevator system works very well, check in moves quickly.Room quality itself actually exceeded my expections. We were placed on the 30th floor (concierge level) with a king room facing the north side of Times Square. The size of the room was about standard for a hotel, which is above average for New York City. The furniture was new and in good condition. There was a 40 inch LG LCD tv. Sofa and bed were all in good shape. The bathroom was not spectacular but the shower was modern. The room had floor to ceiing windows to showcase the view.There were two negatives about the room. The first was a rather musty sort of smell that was vaguely of smoke--now the whole hotel is smoke free. It wasn't overpowering or awful, and I do have a particularly sensitive nose for these things, but I nonetheless noted it. I ended up not changing rooms because we liked the location of it and everything else was fine, but I did give it some consideration.The second negative was light from the atrium (interior) side. The room was remarkably quiet given the location--exterior noise was highly muffled, and even the rooms themselves were unusually quiet for a hotel like this. There was, however, a great deal of light coming in from under the door which made the room rather bright. Now putting something by the door would easily take care of this, but I noted it anyway.Also note that there are no vending machines--however, complimentary water bottles are in the bathrooms. The maid service was unusually good---the room was very thoroughly cleaned each day. There was also turndown service, and all towels were replaced (we took showers in the afternoon after a morning of touring NYC) which was a nice touch.Overall, I would certainly recommend this hotel. If I visited New York on business every week, I may not want to stay here, but for tourists or visitors to midtown, its a very pleasant place to stay which uniquely good views and high quality rooms.

<Author>Bellarina126
<Content>Seamless stay over holiday weekend First of all, let me preface this by saying that I come to New York at least once a year for vacation. I have stayed at several Times Square hotels, as well as The Plaza and other boutique hotels throughout Manhattan. I found the Marriott Marquis to be above average in every single aspect of my stay. I arrived at the hotel at 10:00am, fully expecting my room not to be ready. It wasn't, but they offered me a standard king room if I wanted to check in immediately. Since I don't spend much time in my room, I agreed. They gave me a room on the 43rd floor that looked down on everything in Times Square. Talk about a room with THE view. The elevator system was easy enough to use, and I appreciated the simplicity of it. No worries about kids pushing all the buttons in the elevator. Just put in your floor and it tells you which elevator to go. I never waited more than a few minutes. The glass elevator can be dizzying, but I just closed my eyes and waited till I arrived on my floor!The beds were incredible, and the room was a good size for Manhattan. I had a king size room, flat screen tv, small loveseat, and desk area with plenty of room to navigate around the room. The bathroom was also standard size. There were Bath and Body Works products in the bathroom, as well as lotion and mouthwash. The in-room internet was $16.95/day, which I think is pricey, considering the lower properties at Marriott and Hilton offer it for free, but it's typical. There are multiple subway stops within a short walking distance of the hotel, which is always a plus for me. Times Square is always crowded, so if you are looking for a quieter stay, you want to stay out of that area anyway. I couldn't hear any of the street noise in my room though, and the shades did an excellent job of blocking out the light. I did not have any problems with this stay, and I could certainly recommend it to anyone looking for a consistent hotel in the middle of everything.

<Content>Another good review Just spent 4 nights at the Marriott Marquis and have nothing special to add to the other happy campers. Stay away from their eggs and ham, though. You can skip Junior's Bakery right across from the hotel -- both the take-out pastries and sit-down breakfasts were disappointing and not worth the hype. The best meal we had was at The Cancun Mexican Restaurant on 8th Ave between 56th  55th. Killer frozen margaritas too!If you take the subway, especially down to WTC and Financial District, be sure to ask the booth attendant which train to take. The stop we wanted was closed for construction and we ended up in Brooklyn. The last time we were in NYC was over 20 years ago, and I have to tip my hat to ex-Mayor Rudy Guliani. The difference is amazing. First of all, the people are much friendlier and open than they were before, very proud of their city and happy to direct and offer tips to tourists. There are police EVERYWHERE! We felt absolutely safe. And the city streets are amazingly clean. I can't wait to go back and do the things we didn't have time for on this trip.The hop on/hop off bus is worth the money. If you want a fun NYC experience, take one of those bicycle rickshaws and hang on!  
<Date>Jun 17, 2008

<Author>Carly82
<Content>Amazing Hotel I have been to New York before but this was the first time I stayed at the Marquis. It really is an amazing hotel and the atmosphere, size and location really captures New York. We were lucky enough to stay on the 44th floor with amazing views. The room was spacious and clean with a good sized bathroom. The highlight of the hotel for me was the lifts! As soon as we arrived we were shown how to work them and then we entered the glass lift and travelled up the centre of the hotel with views of each floor as you go! It was like a mini fairground ride!The hotel has several restaurants, bars, a theatre and a revolving restaurant/bar on the top floor! Apparently this is the only one in New York and it takes about an hour to do one rotation - with great views.We ate at the restaurant on the 8th floor - delicious pizza and it was great to watch Times Square from above. The View (rotating restaurant/bar) does get very busy - especially at the weekend, so it is worth booking or getting there early.All the staff were really helpful and charming.The location of the hotel is ideal to explore all of New York. With the subway on your doorstep if you want to travel further afield. I really couldn't say a bad word about this hotel!

<Author>KlingonWarrior
<Content>King of Times Square I have no idea how anyone could rate this hotel as anything except 4 or 5 unless one is expecting something unreal. The Marriott Marquis is a giant hotel right on Times Square. People are everywhere, duh!!! But so are great restaurants, delis, theaters, and shopping---all within ten casual minutes by foot. Buy an unlimited MetroCard for $24 and you get seven days of unlimited subway and bus. One of the major transportatiojn hubs is on 42nd and Broadway, which is 5 minutes away if you walk slowly. BTW, the subway system is fantastic---fast, frequent, clean, and goes virtually everywhere. The maligned elevator system is actually marvelous. Never had to wait more than a couple of minutes. EVER. Two Starbucks on the premises, a huge atrium and lounge to enjoy your coffee or drink and a Junior's Bakery across the street for fancier pastries and New York's Best Cheesecake. BTW, TKTS (which is the discount outlet for that evening's Broadway shows) is currently at the Marriott while their permanent office is being renovated across the street. Another perk! Here's a tip--if you like Chinese food, NY's Chinatown is quite good and the cheapest of any large city I have ever visited.If this sounds like a NYC fan talking, it is, but prior to this visit...not so much. I was fully prepared to dislike the city but could not. NYC just plain WORKS and other cities like San Francisco in particular could learn a lot from the Big Apple. We stayed for eight days and every day was chock full of activities and sights---the Metropolitan Museum of Art being a close second only to the Louvre in the world, IMHO. Back to the Marquis...asked for and got a TSq view on the 33rd floor. Beds OK, bath fine and the space very generous by NY standards. Concierges could be a little more helpful but with 2000 rooms, they are overwhelmed on occasion. Never heard outside noise from the street but did occasionally hear doors and drawers slamming next door. Arrived at 9:00 am from SF on the redeye and immediately were allowed to check in! Then on departure, we requested late checkout (another redeye flight) and stayed until 1:00pm. Great service, I'd say. In summary, this hotel is PERFECT for the first time NYC visitor and for everyone wanting to be in the middle of the party.

<Author>Lilibribri
<Content>Good New York experience We just got back from two nights at the Marriott Marquis in New York to celebrate our 10 year anniversary. We stayed at the Marquis using reward points. Our view was fabulous, right over the North side of Times Square looking right at all the flashy billboards, fun to look at at night, and although they were so bright that it always looked like daylight we just shut the curtains and that took care of that.... it was surprisingly quiet in our room on the 30th floor, we thought for sure we would hear hustle and bustle all night but it was very quiet...... only complaint about room was that the windows are in need of a washing, not an easy task in New York City I am sure...One complaint I have was the ticket booth (which I don't think is even part of Marriott, the box offices just happen to have a window in the Marriott) the people there were not very friendly, they did not even seem to want to help us... our questions were pretty much just ignored as the people at the desk joked amongst themselves, we had better luck going right up to the individual theatre box offices... on thrusday and friday nights we just walked up and down Broadway to the box offices and on Thursday night we walked up to the window of Rent at 8:00 (showtime) and got 8th row tickets for half price and on friday afternoon we walked up to the box office at Phantom of the Opera around 4:00 and got front row center tickets (actor had just handed them in).... so if you just want to wing it and not picky take a walk and chance the box offices....Overall our trip was fabulous and would stay again at the Marriott Marquis (with reward points of course)!!

<Author>Amaklo
<Content>Very impressed with the Marquis I've been to New York many times and have always stayed at smaller hotels, but I was curious about how the enormous Marriott Marquis could warrant the raves here. I had a business conference scheduled nearby, so this was the perfect opportunity to give the Marquis a try. My personal preference is still for a smaller hotel, but I have to say I'm very impressed. The location cannot be beat. The people who work there are uniformly pleasant, well-informed and professional. I had a corner room which was huge, especially by NY standards. The bed was very comfortable and the room was quiet (of course I was on the 27th floor facing the Hudson River, not Times Square). The elevator system is very efficient and I rarely waited more than a couple of minutes. The Times Square TKTS booth is attached to the hotel. There are airport check-in kiosks and a Starbucks near the reception desk (which is on the 8th floor). Subway, buses and taxis are right outside any of the numerous front doors. If I were recommending a place to stay for a first-time visitor to New York, I would not hesitate to suggest the Marquis.

<Author>FamilyTravelSeries
<Content>Don't Spend Your Own Money! This is a great hotel, if you're staying on somebody else's dollar. It's got everything you want - for a price. If you can afford it, go for it. The location is in the heart of Times Square, so all prices are inflated, but the Marriott Marquis assumes most of its guests are business travelers and can spend money like water. I stayed there because of a business convention, so I fit their profile. Want to use a computer at the hotel's business center? $32 per hour. Have a glass of wine in the bar? $13 or more. (In fact, the wine list includes one wine I often buy at home for $8.99 a bottle. They charge $48 for the same bottle.) Yet they refused to honor the credit card I tried to check in with, because it had the name of my company on it, even though they had accepted it to guarantee my reservation. I was forced to use a personal credit card. They can afford to have that attitude because there's a demand for high end service in that location. Honestly, though, I've stayed in lots of of hotels just as good and with a nicer attitude, but at half the price. I'll stay here again next year ... but only if my employer is paying the bill. Next time I'm in NYC (in about three months) I'll stay elsewhere, where the prices are rational and the people are friendlier -- because it will be MY money.

<Author>leftylanza
<Content>Typical Marriott. Great location, typical accommodations. First, let me say that I am a Marriott employee. I love the company's hotels and accommodations. Every time I stay at a Marriott, the service is the same: friendly and helpful. Having said that, the Marriott Marquis Times Square New York lives up to the expected Marriott service level, but isn't really anything more than the typical Marriott property. In fact, there are more comfortable Marriott hotels around the country than the Marquis. What you get at this particular hotel, however, is the location. It is perfectly located in Times Square on Broadway between 46th and 47th.It is expensive to stay at the Marquis, although I got a discount for being an employee. The first floor lobby isn't really the lobby. You have to go up to the 8th floor to check in. Weird, huh? There are a bunch of high speed elevators in a circle that take you up through the hotel, but you might wait a while because there are so many people going up and down. The room was a typical king standard room. I had a partial view of Broadway and a lovely view of an office building. The bed was comfortable, but not nearly as much as some of the other Marriott properties I've stayed at . I don't think this room was equipped with the new Revive bedding that can be found at many other Marriott properties. The bed is why I love staying at Marriott's, and this one wasn't as good as the others. The plasma TV was very nice though, and the channel list included HD channels.As I said, the location was great. It was wonderful coming back from seeing a broadway show and walking to our hotel, in the midst of the throngs of people. I always wanted to be one of those people who could just veer off the path and walk into the hotel. I must say, it was wonderful. The hotel was quiet, once you're in your room, and the accommodations were comfortable. The prices for everything were ridiculous, of course, since you're in Times Square, but what else do you expect? Overall, the hotel was a typical Marriott. Nice design, great location, comfortable room and friendly staff, but nothing spectacular. The best part was being in Times Square.

<Author>bruinTraveller
<Content>An experience in itself For those who are looking to visit New York City for a day or two, this hotel cannot be beat. There are many things that make the Marriott Marquis the greatest hotel in Times Square, but the #1 by far is the location. It is located directly in the dead center of Times Square, making basically everything in short walking distance. The hotel features an incredibly convenient and smart elevator system which makes getting to your room in a hotel with an incredible number of rooms an easy process. On the main floor area there is a very lovely sushi restaurant, and a complete bar area with a wide range of exotic drinks and a glass-wall intimate-table-seating area that directly overlooks Times Square, giving you a view of the nightlife while chatting with friends. All rooms also overlook Times Square, so a great view is never too far away from you. For those of you who are musical theater enthusiasts, the hotel offers a ticket booth where you can inquire about showtimes, locations, even buy tickets right there at the hotel (though with a rather high service charge). Also, the Marquis plays host to The Drowsy Chaperone itself. Service was excellent, we requested a rollaway bed for our room which was promptly delivered, and the staff was always ready to answer any questions we had. Parking was valet, and convenient in every way. The hotel also offers a huge exercise facility, but we didn't get the opportunity to use it. I should mention that this hotel is a great idea for a short-term trip, since the rooms are quite expensive. For a longer stay in New York, I imagine there are more affordable locations, but for a short-term, amazing experience, the Marquis isn't just a place to stay, it will become a memorable part of your experience altogether. (I recently visited NYC again, and even though I didn't stay AT the Marquis, I still went there just for the bar and restaurant!)

The elevators zooming up and down (our girls compared them to the vacuum chutes used by drive-in banks to send transactions to your car) with the different colored lights on each were a sight to behold!The concierge at the desk directed us to the elevator pad, and the adventure began. The elevators are on a sort of reservation system: You press the floor you are requesting on the pad, and a letter appears, telling you to go to that specific elevator - how cool is that? The girls worked out a system as to when each would have a turn to 'call the elevator'.We arrived on the 8th floor, which is comprised of the lobby of the hotel, several restaurants, a concierge desk, a bell desk, lounges, gift shop and travel offices (American Express, Ticket offices, etc.). We arrived at 3:35, and waited in line for about 5 minutes to check in. Our girls sat on a bench near the elevators with their necks craned because the elevator bank is a huge circular structure in the middle of the hotel. All rooms are situated on the outside of the 'hallway' and the inside of the hallway gives a view all the way down to the first floor or all the way up to the 47th floor. Our older daughter told my husband that she could go home now, she was so amazed!While checking in, the reservations agent asked our business there, and I told her it was my husband's birthday. She immediately gave us a voucher for free breakfast buffet (up to $60) at the Atrium Lounge!? Amazing! We had a Times Square View room (towards Central Park) on the 32nd floor. It looked like we could reach out and touch the ginormous billboards outside when we opened our curtains! Our luggage arrived within 15 minutes of our arriving at our room and the bellhop took the time to orient us to where we were, pointed out MM World to us, told us that the Minskoff Theatre was directly across the street (we saw 'The Lion King' matinee the next day) and told us about all of the amenities of the hotel.We just walked around the lobby and gawked (there were several conventions there, but we never felt rushed or crowded). We dressed for dinner and took the elevator down to the 2nd floor to get the express elevator to the 47th floor. The View Restaurant was exquisitely wonderful, on Friday night! The prices were exactly what we'd expect for the service, food quality, view and experience. For a prie fixe of $67.50 per meal (the girls split their meal), we ate WELL - and my husband had several wait staff sing 'Happy Birthday!' to him - BY NAME, to the total delight of our girls!Breakfast at the Atrium Lounge on Saturday morning at 9:30 am was beyond yummy - fabulous service, excellent selections and variety, great omelettes made to order and freshly made waffles and pancakes brought to your table! Oh, My!We had room service for 4 for dinner (after the play and a bicycle rickshaw ride around Central Park), and our food was delivered within 25 minutes of ordering - on a Saturday night?!Overall, we have traveled the world - with and without children - our experience at the Marriott Marquis was one in a lifetime! We are already planning our next trip there! Go Marriott!!!

<Author>visitDC
<Content>Consistently good place to stay I attend a Convention for a week every January and have stayed at a lot of hotels in Times Square. Of all of the hotels I've stayed in, I prefer the Marriott Marquis. The rooms are much bigger than others in the same area, the fitness center is free, the elevators are efficient (now that they've finally finished renovating them), and the staff is nice. Plus, the beds and pillows are really comfortable! If you are visiting Times Square, the Marriott is right in the middle of everything. But if you're there on business, you'll find that the hotel has a nice lounge on the eighth floor for an after-dinner drink, two Starbucks (first floor and eighth floor) for that morning cup of coffee, and is pretty quiet considering it's a huge hotel right in the middle of New York.I have stayed there at least three times that I can remember and have always had good experiences. I highly recommend the Marriott for both business and pleasure!

The beds are a bit small so this year we brought an airbed and comforter for DS which we placed between the 2nd bed and the window, DD was with me and DH got a bed to himself... it worked out GREAT. Again there wasn't a single problem with the elevators.A HUGE plus to theater goers, or any visitor at all, is the fact that the Marquis now has a TKTS booth directly on the side of the building (where people can purchase 50% off same day Broadway and Theater tickets if you are OK with a hit or miss situation. Rolls and bagels with butter are available on almost every corner for a great breakfast (its what many NY'ers do).Today we traveled a bit and all shared 2 slabs of ribs for lunch at the small but exceptional top rated RUB restaurant in Chelsea. For most, it would feel indifferent.For its price (it cost us a whopping $10,000+ USD for our entire stay), it should feel a lot better than 'nice'. Amongst the 2002 rooms, you feel like a robot, especially seeing as you quickly realise that the Marquis is heavily biased towards their business customers. This feels overwhelmingly like a businessmen hotel, and you'll meet many of them as you go up and down the elevators.The hotel is overpriced, even for a hotel ($7 bottled water connected to actual sensors that bill your account if they are off the stand for more than 30 seconds) and $117 USD for a sickening in-room breakfast for 2 adults and a child.Another example.. it cost just over $16 for one 4-second call to Australia to ask a family member to call us back.The hotel is also happy to overcharge. You can either decide to challenge it or not. They will pretend that these charges are natural.Being a beginner to New York, you believe that a hotel in the middle of Times Square screams convenience and taste. While this is in some ways true, you quickly realise that a hotel a couple of blocks down, off broadway or at least out of times square could save you several thousands, for simply having to walk an extra 5 minutes. I must stress this.A Times Square hotel also sounds inviting to those who are looking for a view, but from our 36th-floor high room which we payed extra for, we had a spectacular view of the back of a bland building (yes, I'm being sarcastic).The hotel is as deceiving as possible.. it forgets to mention the (just over) $80 USD tax it charges (PER DAY), $3 per day OCC/JAV charge, it charges $16.95 per day for internet if you request it - but upon scanning for WiFi hotspots, they were plentiful from our room, including the hotel's own WiFi hotspot (in essence.. don't bother paying for internet), and the hotel held $5000 on our credit card (followed by more) from the first day we stayed here.Another problem.. cable/satellite television quit working for the entire hotel several times during our stay, staying offline for several hours - especially in the mornings. Speaking of television, we couldn't find any ports to plug in our cameras to view our video and photos we had taken for the day, and the speakers are located in an awkward position, leaving sound muffled.But while the cable was down, we had enormous fun watching the hotel's 3 self-advertisement channels (there's that sarcasm again.. but hey, they do actually have their own advertisement channels.. and the actors are all business men and women..)On arrival, they had forgotten to leave our New York, New York and A Taste of Starbucks packages in the room, but they were reasonably quick in bringing it up. We ordered this from the last-minute soliciting e-mail they send you before your stay. I've gotta say, it's not worth it at all. Save your money.The hotel isn't big on details, nor guiding those who are new here.. we paid extra for a Stay for breakfast package, which entitled us (we quickly learned the 4 year old is counted as a party, so only two adults would be able to eat, or one adult and the child) to paid-for breakfast each morning.Upon checking in, we were asked what breakfast option we would like, and were invited to pay an extra $100 per day. They weren't clear on the options, so we just stuck to what we had paid for. One morning, we went down to Encore (naturally, being the only restaurant serving breakfast.. though, we weren't told this) and entered the restaurant, not knowing exactly how to use our package. We asked a desk clerk, who asked for our room number. 'Over there', we were instructed. We were seated, and given a menu. This was confusing because I had thought we paid for a buffet. I wasn't sure whether to serve ourself or wait for someone to come over to us. After some confusion, we quit, and left to get some easy breakfast. This isn't a hotel for the inexperienced. We rang the front desk and asked if we could quit or exchange our breakfast portion of the package.. they denied both requests.Security is also inconsistent.. They have fairly useless doormen and greeters (greeting you sometimes) who also seem to act as some sort of low-level security. They also have what looks to be a security desk that doesn't seem to do a lot, other than likely looking for obvious madmen running around with guns. One night, when returning, everyone was required to show their keycards to use the elevators to go up. This was the only real security we've faced, but at the same time it was also inconvenient and felt odd considering it was only on that night. I'm not sure if this is because of a security incident in the hotel or because they just felt like it.We also learned on the 7th night that you should actually key in your floor number into the elevator system for each person (for instance, type '36' three times if there is three of you going to that floor). I'm sure no one does this, but this is what should be done to apparently have their system work optimally.The hotel unfortunately does nothing to make you feel as if your money has been well spent. This is not luxury.. it is just a nice hotel in an excellent location. And that's something that you actually DO NOT need (or at least, do not need to pay this much for). Don't fool yourself into thinking otherwise.This hotel is a nice treat for all of the businesses paying for their employees to a stay here... but it's an excellent waste of the business's money, from that standpoint.One last note which has been covered in other reviews.. the ambience, design and feel of the hotel in public areas isn't what we expected. It just isn't that great, especially seeing as it's Christmas. Bland best describes it.I would seriously consider my other options next time. This is just an honest review and 2 cents from 2 different adult travelers sharing a room (with a child).It's too hard to consider the few good points about the hotel when you're being ripped off daily.The nicest experience we had in this hotel was actually our friendly housekeeper, who we accordingly gave good tips to. (Thank you Hesena).Other minor problems? Power outlets were flimsy, the toilet clogs easily, the coffee machine didn't work, the remote control for the TV gave up and we found a woman's nail on the floor.The best part of our deal at the hotel is that we joined their membership program and asked for airline points, rather than Marriot reward points. Phew!

<Author>oliver5125
<Content>Right in the heart of NYC We booked a room overlooking Times Square and it is well worth the extra charge. The view is mesmerising. Paid $489 - $523 per night and great value at that. This hotel is so centrally placed, the lifts are a thrilling experience in themselves, and the staff are very courteous and helpful. The 38-storey atrium is spectacular. A drink in The View lounge at the top is interesting, but the bars on check-in level on the 8th Floor are more comfortable. This hotel really made our 5 nights in NYC - we would recommend it to anyone. One word of warning - when charging meals and drinks to your room it is easy for someone to overhear your name and room number and take advantage later. Also, mistakes can be made - a $400 meal in the restaurant was charged to our account and it took 20 minutes to have the bill rectified. The explanation was that it was someone with the same name staying in another room and they got the numbers mixed up. For your trip home, hire a stretch limo at the front desk - about $160 to Kennedy and a great way to end your stay.

<Content>Beyond Expectations My sister and I booked a four night stay at the Marriott Marquis Times Square at the last minute. Our decision to stay at this hotel was a list minute one. The hotel itself is quite busy on the ground level and around the elevators, but we felt that the bell boys, desk staff...everyone was friendly and willing to assist us. We ordered room service breakfast several times (try the hot chocolate!) and sampled the breakfast buffet in the restaurant on the 8th floor - both were delicious and the convenience was ideal. Speaking of the restaurant on the 8th, we also had two very quick dinners before rushing off to Broadway and the food is excellent. It's a bit pricey but you can't beat the convenience -- and both meals were miles better than several that we had had out in the city! We enjoyed the Encore Lounge's comfy couches and refreshing beverages - why line up for a loud annoying bar in Times Square when you can relax in peace at the hotel lounge? The gift shop and Broadway ticket booth were also a nice surprise and the next time, I plan to use that amazing gym!And we LOVED the quiet glass elevators. All the theatres are close by, and the addition of Juniors across the street now means there is a fast, cheap, convenient restaurant nearby for a quick bite before the theatre if you can鈥檛 be bothered walking down to 9th street (give the 8th floor lobby restaurant in the hotel a miss as it鈥檚 way are too pricey for the food you get).Although the business centre and phone call costs are expensive they are comparable to other hotels of this calibre ($2 per call and $8 per 15 minutes for internet access). US travellers can get around this by bringing their mobiles and laptops.As for complaints about the lift system it is quite straight forward to use and manages lift load balance. Basically you punch in your floor number and it tells you which lift to go to (not really rocket science!). The upside of this system is you never encounter a lift that is too full to get in which I really appreciated.Every staff member at this hotel is friendly and superbly professional and nothing is too much trouble.We had a wonderful time and highly recommend this hotel to anyone considering spending time in the Times Square District.

You have to go to the 3rd floor and take the express elevator to the 48th floor. But once you arrive it takes your breath away. Certain elevators only go to certain floors, so we could not directly get to the concierge floor without taking the elevator all the way to the lobby and then back up, which was quite annoying when you just want your breakfast or a quick snack.The concierge lounge was also disappointing to us. It was not as large and there was not as big of a selection of food at breakfast as what we have had at other Marriott concierge lounges. Although it was still nice to have access to the free snacks and breakfast.The workout/fitness center was very cool. It over looks Times Square, so you can watch the action while you work out.Like I said before the best part about this hotel is the fabulous location. The half off ticket booth for Broadway shows is literally at the base of the hotel on the street level and the theaters are also within a 5-15 minute walk. The nearest subway stop is less than a 5 minute walk away. There are tons of choices for restaurants and entertainment since you are in the middle of Times Square. If you are a taxi person, there is a huge line of people waiting for taxis at the hotel starting around 5pm. It would be faster to walk or take the subway if you have to travel at rush hour.

<Author>jasperpanda
<Content>location location location Spent a week at the Marriott Marquis, Aug 5-12th. This was our third stay in four years. I had contemplated staying out of the Times Square area this time ,just for a change, but got such a good rate(husband is an airline employee) and knew how good the hotel is so decided to stay again. I don't know how much simpler it can be than pushing the floor you want to go to into one of the many keypads by the elevator and then going to the elevator you are assigned to. Our biggest wait was 3 minutes on Saturday night when we were headed to the theater. I have waited longer in buildings in Vancouver and in different hotels in many different cities. I just don't get the problems people claim to have had on this site.Workout room - outstanding! It's too bad it is in a city like NYC where you more than get your share of exercise from so much walking! But it is worth using, no matter how exhausted you are.Location - amazing. Yes it is in the heart of Times Square, but that is why I have come to New York! You can take less crowded streets (stay off Broadway) to get around once you tire of battling the crowds on Broadway. The weekends are the worse but it still would not deter me from staying there again. All the theaters arewithin walking distance,( some literally across the street or in the hotel), and since I did some ticket lotteries to see the shows and bought Standing room for others it was very convenient to go to the theater at 5ish to get our tickets, dash home to change and head back up for show time. This was the first year I got SR tickets and what a deal, I would do it again in a heartbeat. The tickets were as cheap as $20 and as expensive as $26!! We had a great view of the performances and did not feel uncomfortable standing at all. I look at it this way, you can wait in the TKTS lineup for up to 3 hours to get discounted tickets or you can show up at the theater a couple of hours before showtime, have no wait and then do the standing during the show. Your day is not interrupted by the afternoon lineup for tickets either.Housekeeping - room was clean but I felt it could have been kept cleaner during our stay. Housekeeper seemed to be looking for tips and kind of got on my nerves. I guess I should have tipped earlier in our stay and maybe would have had better results. I also found they made a lot of noise in halls on a couple of mornings. There is a 3 hour time difference for me and 08 NY time is 5 am where I live! But the housekeeping issue really is very petty and it would certainly not prevent me from returning.Concierge - helpful, some more than others. Especially Kelly and Zoe, who were great.

<Author>WIWOL92
<Content>Good hotel but for the elevators We stayed here for 4 nights on another trip to catch some shows; hence location was everything. Check in was very easy, with our being shepherded to the Elite line to avoid a minor jam at the desk. Upgrade to a corner room for $50 per night was accepted and the check in clerk (Jonathon) was extremely helpful and attentive. The room, on the 41st floor, proved very spacious and well worth the extra cost. There were 3 drawbacks with the hotel, which spoiled an otherwise very good stay. Firstly, the lack of a refrigerator in the room was annoying considering there was a yawning space in the bureau shouting out its need to be filled by such an item. However, the ice machine wasn't too far a walk and the daily $10 tip left under the pillow meant the maid was delivering ice cold bottles of water at every opportunity. (Could be bought for $4(?) in the room.) The second point concerned soundproofing between rooms - it seemed very limited. Having heard every word of conversations in the adjoing room, we ended up speaking in whispers! Finally, the point that has already deterred us from booking the Marriott for our next trip and has been mentioned by many other guests - the elevators. The pre-allocation of a lift on selection may look like a very efficient way to transport guests to so many floors, but it is also very frustrating and time consuming. The lack of indicators to show where the cars are means no judgement can be made on anticipated wait time, which increases the feeling of frustration. Waits of 15 minutes were usual - at virtually any time of day - and, at one stage, we seriously contemplated walking down all 40 storeys as we were concerned about making 'curtain up'!

<Author>Catwoman62
<Content>Great room, great location if you're looking for the action I stayed at the Marriott Marquis from Augst 1-3rd. It took over an hour to get from the airport (LGA) at 4pm to the hotel, and most of the time the taxi just crawled along. Love that rush hour traffic! I knew that I needed to go to the 8th floor, and as soon as I approached the elevators, a man in a red Marriott coat asked if I were checking in, (I was pulling two suitcases, so it was a wise supposition on his part!) and led me over to show me how the elevators worked. Since almost everyone else comments, let me throw my two cents in about the elevators. If you take 2 seconds to learn how the system works, it's a piece of cake! Simply input your floor number, and check to see which letter elevator the system directs you to. I never waited more than 2 minutes for an elevator. There were several clueless people who just wandered on elevators at random and then wondered why there were no buttons to push. If you glance at the panel in the door as you enter the elevator, it shows you which floors it's going to stop on. I never stopped at more than 3 before my own floor.Anyway, check-in was one of the fastest processes I've ever undergone, and I told the woman so. She was welcoming, and cheerful. I was on the 22nd floor, in a corner king-bed room (2258). The view was of the Hudson River and bunch of rooftops so not all that glamorous, but by looking straight down I could see several theaters, including the one where 鈥淎 Chorus Line鈥?is playing. The room was particularly spacious for New York, and had a couch, easy chair with footstool, cocktail table, two floor lamps, a desk with a rather uncomfortable chair, a king-sized bed with a padded bench at its foot, and an armoire into which was tucked the tv. Another reviewer was right 鈥?the tv does pull out, but doesn't really swivel so it's difficult to watch the tv from any comfortable angle. I ended up sitting on the end of the bed to watch it. There was a short passage behind the bed to get to a small table on which the coffee machine sat, the closet, which had a large safe in it, and the bathroom which was spotlessly clean and had nice touches like two soapdishes, one of which was up high, a rain-shower type shower fixture, and a curved shower curtain bar, to give you extra room when you're in the shower and you don't have to touch the curtain. I've forgotten the name of the upscale shampoo/etc. but those don't usually impress me. There were plenty of towels, and while they were a bit on the skimpy and rough side, they were also spotless. There was water still in the coffee machine, which turned me off, so I never did use it. I'm not a coffee drinker anyway, but did want to have some tea. I had requested foam pillows instead of feather, and indeed, they had foam pillows on the bed. This room has a connecting door to the room next door.I was traveling with a colleague from work 鈥?she had a room on the 33rd floor. The first night we went to the Bombay Palace on W. 52nd Street (see my review) and had little trouble catching a cab back. The valets at the hotel are wondeful about catching cabs 鈥?there is a taxi stand just outside the main entrance where you can line up, and they will hail them for you. My only negative experience in the trip came at the end of our second day 鈥?it took us 45 minutes to find an available cab to get back to the hotel, but that's not the hotel's fault. We were hot, tired, and cranky by that point, and definitely not in the mood to deal with any more crowds of people, so we elected to just eat at the Encore restaurant on the 8th floor near the main desk. I had a wonderful chicken pot pie in a huge souffle dish, and my friend had the chicken francaise which she said was ok. Our waiter Bob was quite entertaining. We both finished with the white chocolate raspberry dome, which was delicious. After dinner we wandered through the Atrium bar over to the Broadway bar, and stood by the windows looking down on Times Square. We thought about staying for a drink, but there were a number of undisciplined brats running around (and this was after 9pm) so we elected not to. I didn't use the fitness center, but it's on the 23rd floor, with great views. Yes, the hotel is expensive (my bill for two nights was just over $1000, booked via corporate travel agent 鈥?presumably you can do much better on something like Priceline), but the location is ideal, particularly if you are interested in Broadway shows. This is peak tourist season, so there were a bazillion people all over the place at all hours of the day and night. I'm not sure I would go back 鈥?I enjoyed my experience, but when I'm traveling, I also like to have a quiet hotel to return to, and between the Starbucks, the ticket office, the restaurants, gift shops, etc, this one is definitely not quiet! I definitely recommend it for someone looking for the Broadway experience, however.

<Author>jdybh
<Content>A Wonderful stay My friend and I stayed at the Marriot on Memorial Day weekend. Our stay was booked through a tour group and the entire visit could only be described as fantastic. This was our first trip to New York and my friend and I had wonderful experiences at the Marriott Marquis. My friend and I like to travel comfortably and not be stressed about transportation, lodging, and meals. So we planned many activities in advance. First, the Marriott has a service where you can book a towncar to pick you up at the airport. We used this service. Our incoming flight was delayed and we notified the hotel of the delay. When we got to the airport the town car representative was not there. We called the hotel and they immediately put me in touch with the car service. Needless to say, the service upgraded us to a six passenger limo (no extra charge) and we had a wonderful ride into the city. When we arrived at the hotel, I made the assumption that since we booked with a tour group our rooms where probably in the back of the hotel with no view. So when checking in I asked how much it would cost to upgrade our room to a times square view room. They upgraded us at no extra charge. My friend and I were so happy. The view from the room was perfect, the beds were to die for, and the bathroom has everything you would ever need. When my friend and I were returning from dinner our first evening, my friend had a headache. The hotel staff were so accomodating and had Tylenol delivered to our room and she also called to ensure we got the medication. When we were returning to our room that first evening, we found our room door open. My friend and I turned around, went back downstairs and approached the hotel staff that helped us with the Tylenol. She called security to meet us at our door. By the time we made it back to our room security was there. Anthony and his team were great, they made sure nothing was missing and inspected the lock on the door. (We later learned that when closing the door if you hit the inside handle it throws the deadbolt, so we made sure to always ensure the door closed before we left). Anthony gave us great information about the city, subways, and things to do. All of his advice was right on. Also, the hotel staff that we notified about our room called again to ensure we were o.k. The Marriott has a taxi line, so you do not have to hail a cab. They will get it for you. The Starbucks on the first floor runs like a well oiled machine. The elevator system ran effciently and we did not have long waits at all. The discount ticket booth to the Broadway shows is right outside the Marriott. If you want to get tickets this way prepare to wait in an extremely long line. (It appeared to be at least 1 to 2 hours). My friend and I had dinner at the View restaurant. The restaurant rotates slowly 360 degrees like the space needle in Seattle. The bill was expensive, but you are paying for the view. They may need to update the restaurant furniture soon though. The furniture was old and worn. But our waiter, view, and food was good. All in all I would highly recommend this hotel. The location you can not beat, The staff was friendly, helpful, and courteous. The maid cleaned our room exceptionally, including organizing our make-up in the bathroom. Your stay will be worth every penny. First time New York Tips: Go on-line and buy the express passes to the Empire state building if the building is on your itinerary. The line is at least two hours long without passes. Be sure that you DO NOT WAIT IN LINE with express passes. These passes allow you to go to front of each and every line going up to the top and returning the bottom. Show your tickets to the staff and they will guide you. One of the staff said to us that the passes were gold and to hold onto them tight. They are $40.00 each but worth every penny unless you like waiting in line and wasting time. We got to the top in about ten minutes. Tip #2 Use the subways. They were nothing like we thought they would be. They are efficient, well lit, clean, and the people we encountered were nice and helpful. The subway is the best way to get around. Tip #3 If you have an interest in eating at the many famous chefs restaurants e.g. Bobby Flay, Mario Vitalle make reservations as for ahead as possible so you will not be disapppointed. Finally, when you do take taxis only take yellow cabs and HOLD ON. I thought we were going to be killed a few times. Have a great time and stay at the Marriott. You will not be disappointed.

<Author>DrumBoy101520
<Content>Perfect Location The Times Square Marriott Marquis is in the heart of Times Square. The hotel is within walking distance of broadway shows, five star dining, and the Times Square (42nd Street) subway station. For tourists, the location of this hotel is better than any other hotel in the city. It will take about thirty minutes to get to the hotel by taxi from La Guardia and about fourty five minutes from JFK. The Marquis just built a workout center that has several cardio machines with personal televisions. I found the View, which is located on the 46th floor of the hotel, to be overly priced. I did not eat at the steakhouse.

<Author>carlareno
<Content>NY's Eve in a Ball-drop room in New York City The hotel itself is pretty much just like any of the other large hotels in Times Square - Westin, W, etc. One interesting fact we discovered is that unlike the surrounding hotels, it isn't unionized! According to the 2 gents from the bell/door staff that told us this, the employees here have better attitudes as a result and hustle for their guests because they get to keep everything they make. I have to say, the staff WAS pretty great - friendly and helpful.First thing about this hotel- it's BIG. Like enormous big. That's fine if you like that type of thing. The public areas are well maintained (lobby, etc.) and the rooms are in decent shape (not great - but decent). It has several restaurants - they are OK (NYC has so many great places to dine why would you eat here unless you had to?). The views from this hotel - those rooms that face Times Square - are fantastic as the rooms have floor to ceiling windows. This is the real selling point for this hotel. If you are interested in doing the whole NY's Eve thing, this is the way to do it in style (but be prepared to pay somewhere in the range of $1700-$2000 for that one night). We called the hotel directly - that's the ONLY way to get last-minute rooms like this one for NY Eve. Evidently each hotel holds a couple of rooms, knowing that folks like us will wait until the last minute. We were on the 17th floor which was great - could still hear the 1 million+ people outside. Security was fantastic - we never worried about this one bit (a major accomplishment given the rowdy crowds). I was surprised that there was no mini-bar or even an in-room refrigerator (but there is a big space in the wadrobe which is designed to accomodate one?). We requested a small in-room refrigerator and were charged for it ($25 a day I think). There is a very nice fitness center overlooking the atrium and a Starbuck's in the lobby so you can get your caffeine fix in the am.

<Author>myhaven
<Content>Surprisingly goos for a Marriot I rated this hotel excellent, considering that it is a Marriot, not my chain of choice. Actually, I avoid chains, but this was the conference hotel and the other reviews on this site put me at ease. First, it is not overwhelming like the NYC version, nor ugly. They manage to successfully differentiate the spaces enough so you don't have to navigate a football stadium, yet you can figure out the lay of the land in one go. Best, it is quiet - they don't torture you with music and there's enough padding to absorb noise. The motor entrance (only way to get in) is pretty miserable and not terribly safe from vehicles should you opt to hoof it. Our room was on the 41st floor, across the hall from the ice machine, which we did not hear. Magnificent bed (not too soft like many luxury beds) and great view. They manage to keep prices low by little omissions, which are worth the trade off - no robes, make-up mirror or mini-bar, e.g. While the reservation staff looked wiped and it was only noon, my rep treated me with the kind of politeness and desire to please that you find in a luxury hotel. In short, you don't feel like you're in a cattle call hotel, which it basically is. Oh - the exercise room is great, and you must travel to a high floor and look down from many vantage points, it's like peering through a kaleidescope.

<Author>mjdallas
<Content>Terrific Locataion, Great Views, Wonderful Beds We used Marriott points for a 6 night stay. We took our 13 year old granddaughter to New York as a gift so this was a special trip for us. My husband is a Marriott Platinum member so we did enjoy some extra benefits. We arrived at the hotel prepared to go to the 8th floor to check in. When we walked in the door we were asked if we were Executive rewards club. My husband said that he was Platinum and as a result we were able to check right in on the first floor. We only went to the 8th floor twice in 6 days-once just to see it and the second time when my husband's key stopped working so we needed to get him another key.The elevators are great if you follow the system. I can see how it can be a little confusing for some people, but we never had a problem. We were told that the elevators never stop at more than 5 floors and while we were there they rarely stopped at more than 3. We did see some people who apparently couldn't figure out the system and they got on the wrong elevator. However the system is simple and we never had a problem with waiting for one and we were always able to get one with a minimum wait.Our room was on the 39th floor with a spectacular Times Square View. The room was clean, large for a New York hotel room, and very quiet. The beds were extremely comfortable and the lighting in the room was very adequate. We opted for the $16.95 internet package. This package is usually $9.95 at other Marriotts around the country, but we were in NYC so we went with the flow. Because of my husband's Platinum status we had access to the Concierge Lounge. The lounge is open Sunday evening and Monday through Thursday and then Friday morning for breakfast. It is closed Friday from about 2:30 until Sunday evening. This was a terrific benefit. Every morning during the week we had breakfast in the Lounge. They served scrambled eggs, fruit, cereal, assorted cold cuts, bagels, three types of whipped cream cheese,yogurt, coffee, pastries and juices. If we had to purchase this same breakfast in one of the hotel restaurants it would have cost us about $18.00 a person. There is a case in the Lounge with assorted juices, yogurt, water and soft drinks. About 5:30 pm they put out appetizers. There were always two hot appetizers, three salads, 4 wonderful cheeses,crackers, rolls, and more fruit. One evening we were so tired from walking all over the city we had the appetizers in the Lounge and skipped dinner. The wine and other alcoholic beverages were more expensive than at other Concierge Lounges around the country. A glass of wine was $10.50 and at other Lounges around the country a glass of wine is usually around $5.50 or $6.50 a glass. At 8:30 they put out dessert and coffee. I highly recommend that you price rooms both on and off the Concierge level. If you aren't an Executive Marriott Rewards member at a level that automatically gives you Concierge Loung privileges and you are going to be staying at the hotel on days that the Lounge is open and if the difference in price isn't too great it would be a benefit to book the Concierge Level room. They also have free wireless computer access in the Concierge Lounge if you prefer not to pay $16.95 a day for access in your room. We have stayed here in the past and would definitely stay here again. You can't beat the location.

<Author>LongtimeinSF
<Content>Excellent location; elevators were OK; We loved our stay!!! We stayed here for several nights in October'06 and really enjoyed the hotel..location, nice rooms (we had awesome view of Times Square), good service and proximity to theaters...First, let me address the elevator issue, which seems to be bothering most reviewers: We stayed at the hotel during the week and I imagine it wasn't sold out, because we didn't experience major waits or crowds by the elevators. The system is odd, but it seemed to have been working fine, at least during our stay. We did notice increased waits on Friday afternoon, but we were checking out already.The rooms: we really liked the rooms, they were spacious, with adequate bathroom space, excellent bedding and even a coffee maker; compared to other 4 star properties we've stayed at in NY, this room was excellent; even realizing that there're other 4-5 star properties out there (not in NY) with more luxurious rooms, this was fine. The location: I was a bit apprehensive about staying right on Times Square, because I remember it being dirty and filled with bums - this was NOT the case. Times Square has changed, it's still very crowded (as to be expected of course), but it's very well maintained, there're tons of restaurants in the vicinity and not a homeless insight (I wish I could say the same about my native SF). More on location: If you come to NY for vacation, Broadway is a must. An extra nice thing about Marriott is that there's a same-day ticket booth for hard-to-get (and other) shows on Broadway right on the first floor of the hotel- the tx are discounted (about 40-50% off). We were able to see as much as time allowed. Other: there're several subway stops right near the hotel; it's close to downtown, all the Midtown tourist attractions, the pier (if you'd like a boat ride), shopping (Macy's, Daffy's, 5th Avenue, etc) and a million restaurants in the area. Overall, I would recommend this hotel. We really enjoyed our stay.

You go to one of many computerized keypad and enter your floor and wait for the computer to direct to a particular elevator letter. IT'S THAT EASY. You just go and wait infront of your elevator for a maximum of 2 or 3 minutes, usually much sooner.4. The rooms are definately some of the largest, cleanest and best kept hotel rooms I have been in. The toilets are a good size  VERY well kept, the beds VERY comfortable, the room VERY clean.5. The staff are the best. Regardless of what time of the day or night, if you call for any kind of problem, regardless of the time, someone is there within 5 minutes.6. Checking in and checking out are a breeze. The staff are very fast and very friendly.7. Breakfast in the hotel, though expensive, (buffet $22.00 adults but $4.50 children) is REALLY good. Lots to choose from and really tasty and CLEAN.8. Bellmen are ALWAYS avaliable, all day long. We booked a bellman for 6:30 am and he was on time without any followup calls. Need a cab? no problem at this hotel. Numerious people are always avaliable to call a cab for you which are lined off outside the building.9. There is a Starbucks on the 8th Floor (limited opening hours) and a larger one on the ground floor which opens early and closes late.This has been the best hotel experience I have ever had. We booked a couple of rooms which were together with a Time Square view, and we have yet to make a complaint that was a true problem.My Advice To You: If the price of this hotel is within your budget, you should trully consider this hotel. You will not be disappointed. Complain? you could always complain. Disappointed? you won't be. Don't forget, the hotel is within walking distance of Broadway shows, most attractions and most shopping areas (Time Square, Fifth Avenue, Fashion Avenue, etc..)Thank you Marriott Marquis New York and thank you Trip Advisor.
