<Author>joshj_146
<Content>Great hotel to be in the middle of times square; good amenities We were looking to go to NYC for 4 days and wanted a hotel that would be right in the thick of things - smack in the middle of Times Square. Being a business traveller, I had to ensure that all rooms were connected to the Internet, which they were. However, Internet was $16.95 USD/day. Check in is @ 3 PM; we got there at around noon. We left our luggage with the bell man and went for lunch. By the time we came back (about 2 PM), the room still wasn't ready. Usually they'd charge you $50/day to have a Times Square view, but the guy at the check in counter gave us that view for free, since they didn't have our original room ready. We asked for a lower floor, and that request was honoured - we were on the 15th floor. Before leaving, I read a lot of reviews here about the elevator situation. Turns out it's all been resolved. In the 4 days we were there, we didn't wait more than a minute for the elevator to arrive - if you use the system correctly. A lot of people don't listen to the staff when they show you how to use them - if you don't know how to use them (which is very simple), you will never get an elevator. The elevators are fast, smooth, and quite nice looking too!The room was very average for a Mariott. It was absolutely nothing special, but it was quite spacious and very clean. The bathroom looked nice, with marble counters, etc. My only complaint about the room was that the bathroom drain took a long time to drain (might have been me not knowing how to use it). Also, there was not very much water pressure during my showers. The food in the hotel was VERY expensive ($39/person for breakfast and lunch combined). We didn't have any food in the hotel, although the bars and restaurants in the hotel looked really good. I'm scared of heights, so we didn't go up to the View (45th floor revolving restaurant). The public areas of the hotel looked brand new - marble everywhere. My favourite thing about the hotel was: the location, and the security. We came back at about 2:30 AM after a night of just walking around an enjoying the nightlife. I was pleasantly suprised to see security waiting on the first floor looking at people's room key before letting them into the hotel. I thought that this was great, especially with how open the hotel is. I can't comment on the prices because a relative of mine is a travel agent so we got a deal. Overall, if you want to be right in the middle of times square, and stay in a hotel with tons of services and very nice staff, the Marquis is surely for you! There are also tons of restaurants and stores

<Author>groupoffour
<Content>Good " times " at the Marquis My husband and I and our teenage son and daughter stayed 5 nights at this hotel at the end of July. It was our second stay there in 2 years. The hotel could not be more convenient to everything as it is in the center of Times Square. We arrived mid morning and were given an early check-in. Clovis, at the front desk ,was most helpful and we appreciated the early check-in as we had travelled all night. The room was clean, quite spacious (bigger than rooms I've stayed in in Seattle, Honolulu, Toronto, Boston etc) and quiet. Yes you could hear some noise from the street, but it did not bother us in the least and we slept very well. The hotel had a rollaway (single mattress size) for our daughter to use . There are blackout curtains that really do the trick and we often slept until 10. (We are from the West Coast and seemed to just stay on that time) You never heard noise from an adjoining room or from the hallway, unbelievable for a hotel that size. The workout room is outstanding, my son and I enjoyed using it at the end of the day, you look down on Times Square from your treadmill and take in all the lights and action from high above. The subway stations are close by, shopping, restaurants all over and the theater within a few blocks. My daughter and I saw Hairspray (wonderful) and Altar Boyz (so so) and my husband and son saw Dirty Rotten Scoundrels ( they won the lottery and paid $26 for their tickets - go to the theater at 4:30 and put your name in). Make an effort to walk over the Brooklyn Bridge, best time is at dusk to see the Manhattan skyline. Staten Island Ferry is free and gives you a wonderful view of Statue of Liberty. We were given a late checkout on the day we left, so along with the early check-in we could not be happier. We would definitely stay here again. Oh, we never experienced any elevator delays at all, at any time of day or night.

<Author>Traveler_VA
<Content>Terrific hotel! We had a great three night stay at the Marriot Marquis. The location of this hotel can't be beat - right in the heart of Times Square, within easy walking distance of subway, big sights, and of course Broadway shows. <Author>Travelmore
<Content>Location Location, location, location.... The Marriot Marquett located on Broadway and 45th Avenue, overlooking Time Square was just perfect for an inexperienced New Yorker. The highlight of the trip was that 1/2 price ticket sales for Broadway shows had relocated to the 46th St. entrance of the hotel. We were able to purchase same day tickets for 50% off. It was very convenient . We saw two shows, The Color Purple and The Odd Couple, both for 50% off.. and the seats were very good! The fitness Center, located on the 23rd floor was very nice. It had a number of treadmills, eliptical trainers, exercise bikes, steppers, free weights and assisted weight machines. Water, towels and head sets were available. The fitness center was open 24 hours/day. Downside was that there was no pool, sauna, whirlpools or steam baths. The hotel does not have a spa. We had a great time in NYC and would be happy to book into the Marquis Times Square for a future visit.

It is Marriotts self-denial about it's ongoing elevator problems which has prompted me to post this review. The rest of the place is fine and more or less as it should be, but there are choices of other nearby hotels with good views and comfortable beds. Marriott should not be so complacent. Customers have choices-and I've made mine, at least until I read on Trip Advisor that this elevator issue has been properly resolved.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Towering Absurdity First, the nearly impenetrable crowds of Times Square tourists make entrance to this hotel an exhausting challenge. (If you were always hoping to see Times Square, you should know that it has become little more than a gigantic outdoor mall - a Sunglass Hut here, Gap across the street, Olive Garden down on the corner). But you've got the energy and the nerve (hey, this is NY!), and you've made it inside! You wait with a dozen other guests (now 15, now 21) for the elevators to your room, or to the check-in desk which is on the eighth floor. The wait is as much as 15 minutes, since the computer system that controls the elevators tends to crash when it gets busy. And it's ALWAYS busy here - there were three conferences going on simultaneously when we were here, and that was less than usual. You're grateful when John shows up in his red double-breasted jacket to excort the now highly impatient crowd to the freight elevators - past the stacked chairs and dusty cases of hotel water bottles. John's nice enough (everyone's nice enough here), and he says simply that this is what happens here when it's busy. That's what the waitress said when she tried to deliver our breakfast 35 minutes late. But don't worry, they'll comp it when it's late. They're used to it. Things here are ALWAYS late. Now you're ready to check out. You stand on the 33rd or 41st floor for 10 minutes, 15 minutes, as the crowd grows, bags in tow, waiting for an elevator to stop at your floor. Slowly the awkward banter goes silent, the humor is gone, and someone goes to call from the nearby emergency phone. They'll send someone soon. They're VERY nice - they're used to it here. The crowd grows. On a floor above, the alarm rings. Uh oh. Someone's having a worse time than you. But at last an elevator stops at the floor, ten of the more ambitious of you squeeze on (hope that alarm doesn't have to ring), and soon you're downstairs, thankful to have made it out alive. Wait on the 50 person line for a cab? No thanks, we'll just walk up to Eighth Ave and hail one ourselves. But the room was nice. Good Luck.

<Rating>5	-1	5	-1	5	-1	5	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Here's the scoop on the elevators... Like most of you, I was kind of concerned about the elevator situation, but wanted to be unbiased. Our family of 4 has travelled all over the world and stayed in 2 star to 5 star hotels. We stayed at Marriott Marquis during Spring Break week so maybe more crowded than usual, though I can't imagine there is every any down time in NYC in the middle of Times Square. The way the elevators work is you walk over to the keypad and press in the floor you wish to go to. After a few seconds, it beeps and a letter appears designating which elevator you should wait for. When it arrives you get in and the elevator stops at all floors which the computer programming has designated your elevator to stop at. In theory, it should be the msot efficient way to handle loads of people going to many different floors. The problem is that I don't think the engineers took into account human nature and how we react when we are waiting for something to happen. First of all, there are no numbers which light up so that you can see which floor your elevator is on. So you may be standing there for only 5 minutes, but it seems a lot longer because you feel helpless with no way to track how long it's going to be before the elevator gets to you, and sometimes you feel like the elevator may have skipped you. I watched a lot of people get frustrated which in turn led to repetitively reeentering their floor number on the keypad. Who knows what that does to the computer programming. Also, if you get disgusted and get on whichever elevator comes next, there are no buttons in the elevator and you are stuck with whichever floor that elevator is programmed to go to. Finally, I think that this hotel just doesn't have enough elevators. We had times when the elevator came quickly and were relatively empty-this only happened during what I would call the non-rush hour times. But during rush hour (like 7:30 to 8:30AM or during the lunch hour or at the end of the day)you could wait for 30 minutes and not get an elevator (happened to my husband). So you end up having to factor in elevator wait time into your travel calculations. As a final example, my daughter and I got back from shopping at 7:15PM and wanted to drop off bags and change before an 8:00 Broadway show which was just 1 block over. 45 minutes seems like a reasonable amount of time to get that done. My husband called me on my cell phone and told me not to come upstairs and just meet him in the lobby or we would never get back down in time for the show and he was right. Sorry for the longwinded review. The Marriott Marquis has a great location with really comfortable and generous sized rooms (especially for NYC), but you just need to be prepared for the elevators!  
<Date>Apr 17, 2006
<Rating>3	-1	4	-1	4	-1	3	-1

The reception is actually on the 8th floor, which requires either an elevator journey (if you can bear the wait) or a longer trek by escalators. Although I was fortunate enough not to experience any major waits for the elevators, others were not so lucky, with 20-30 minute delays appearing to be quite common, meaning you needed to allow extra time at peak periods such breakfast and dinner times. I'm not sure what the hotel can do to rectify the situation, but perhaps if the elevators were more functional and had greater capacity than the glass-backed ones they have at present, the situation might be alleviated.All in all, not a bad hotel, but I'd probably seek out somewhere else if I stayed in NYC again.

<Author>Goldenoak
<Content>Location Is NOT Everything!!! We just completed a 6 night stay at the Marriott Marquis, February 23 through March 1, 2006. The location, in the heart of Times Square, is quite nice. The problem seems to be outside traffic coming into the hotel and the elevator system cound not handle the high volume of traffic. The front desk staff at this hotel could use a bit of customer service training but again, a lot of the problem seems to be with the amount of guests they try to handle. We had the Sunday Brunch in The View which is excellent, both the food and the view of NYC. We had room service dinner and this was also quite good. Probably would not stay at this hotel again mainly due to the elevator problems and the staff not being up to par in terms of customer service. Our room was great, wonderful view of Times Square. We've selected the Doubletree suites in Times Square for our next NYC trip.

<Author>LittlePinkSequin
<Content>We won't go back We stayed at the Marriott Marquis because a friend recommended it to us, and we were very disappointed. The hotel is nice (I guess), the rooms were clean (all the major requirements were met), but it's very inconvenient, and we would not stay here again.First, the elevators--what a MESS. Several were out of order during our trip, and because of the unique way they arrive (you're assigned to an elevator based on your floor; you cannot just choose any elevator), you get to move whenever YOUR elevator arrives. If you're assigned to M, and every other elevator arrives but M, you wait. Those elevators aren't going to your floor, and there is no panel inside so you can't hop on a different lift and press your floor. If it's not programmed to go there, it won't go there. If you're on the 36th floor, this is a problem. They tell you to schedule an extra 15 minutes just to get out of the hotel!Second, the location is horrible (in my opinion), because we did not enjoy staying in Times Square. Again, what a mess. Times Square is great to visit--then get the hell out. You're not immediately next to a subway entrance, so you have to maneuver through the crowds to find one.Third, the hotel is just way too big. It hosts huge conferences, so it can turn into a zoo quickly.Fourth, yes, our room was clean--maybe too clean. Housekeeping kept using this orange-scented cleaner that was so strong, we couldn't breath. Even after we asked them not to use it or just don't clean our room everyday--we're not sloppy, we don't mind--they still orange-ized our room. Minor complaint, but after everything else, we found it very annoying.The nice thing about this hotel (yes, there is one) is the View bar. We loved it. Definitely check it out. But you don't need to be a guest to go, so stay somewhere else and just pay the cover.Will you hate this place? Probably not. But you can do better.Previous to this, we stayed at the Park Central across from Carnegie Hall and were much happier. Smaller, convenient, clean, right next to a Subway entrance (you'll appreciate this), no huge masses of people to navigate... And at night, we could hear the horses' hooves from the Central Park buggies--a nice touch.

<Author>Souette
<Content>Great Stay for New Year's Eve! Chose this hotel due to prime location in Times Square for New Years Eve. I made an extra effort to note the elevator service due to previous reviews on this site.I was on the 21st floor and my average wait time for an elevator was 20 seconds...even with numerous guests waiting. The most I waited was 3 minutes. On the elevator touch pad, you enter your floor number and the pad immediately displays which elevator to board ( ex: I, J, K, L, etc). There was either one or two hotel workers standing by the key pad to assist those who were new to the system.Check-in and check-out was less than a 3 minute wait and all workers were courteous  smiling. The hotel was booked solid and quite busy in all area but since the hotel is HUGE, I didn't feel hurried or cramped.Rooms were of average size but the bedding was wonderful. So soft and relaxing. The bathroom was of fair size but the bathtub was a joke. Probably no more than 12-15 inches deep, so a nice soaking bath after sightseeing would be out of the question. There are several chain stores such as Olive Garden, Hard Rock available within 2-3 blocks or you could choose a little hole-in-the-wall pizza joint as well. Several Broadway theaters were within a block or two for a 5 minute walk from the Marquis. You can also walk 5-10 minutes and be out of the hustle of Times Square and visit the family-owned shops  restaurants.The hotel also has a revolving restaurant/bar on top and I recommend that you visit this at night. Amazing views. Be sure to tell your waiter that you are a hotel guest so the $7 cover charge is waived. You can eat from the buffet for $27.95. I did and the food was good. Although it was pricey, the view made it worth it. If your stay is all about location, location, location, I recommend the Marriott Marquis because the service  bedding is an added plus.

<Author>kurock_chalk
<Content>I'll be back. Clean, quiet, great bed, good views, fabulous Cosmopolitans, convenient Starbucks, best showerhead and working elevators. Our stay was perfect. Let me take a moment and explain the elevator system. Go to the correct set of elevators, the floor numbers are on the entryway wall. Enter your floor number into the system, an electronic version of pushing the up button. The system will show you which elevator car to go to, for example enter floor 8 and the system tells you to go to car B. If you enter a floor number and double XXs appear, the system is overloaded and the elevators have individual attendents that will stop on each floor as called. We found the system overloaded only in the evening rush hour. Everything else about the stay was perfect.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The elevators are a nightmare Don't stay at this hotel unless you want to wait at least 15 minutes everytime you use the elevator. When I complained to a manager, she told me the average wait, before renovations started, was 30-45 minutes, and that we were lucky we were only waiting 20. There are 13 elevators, two of which only serve the restaurant on the top floor, and two were being renovated, so 9 elevators were serving 5000 guests. Not a pretty sight. Time is much too precious on a trip to New York to waste it waiting for elevators. I travel to New York once or twice a year, and I'd like people to know this is not representative of most other hotels in New York. I was attending a conference, and the facilities were excellent. Our room was clean and beautiful. The food served at the conference was wonderful. The staff was friendly and helpful, except for the manager previously mentioned, but I'd never recommend this hotel to anybody.

The restaurants and room service were outrageously expensive ($60 price fixe dinner, $15 for 3 muffins from rm serv stick out in my mind) but you can probably expect that from any Times Sq/NYC location. The fitness room was really nice and huge, lots of machines, equipment, etc and is free for guests. All of the staff were very nice and helpful. Save yourself $10/night and skip the valet and park in the garage directly across the street (where they end up parking your car for you anyway). Now on to the hot topic - elevators. We had NO PROBLEMS WITH ELEVATORS! However, we were only on the 10th floor - request a low floor when making reservation and you'll be ok. Anyway, we also took trips up to the top floor lounge, gym, etc., came in  out of the hotel during the day, late  early and never waited more than 5 min for an elevator. *Tips for Breakfast: Paramount Cafe, Tick Tock Diner - Lunch/Dinner: Tir Na Nog, Lazzara's Pizza (wkdays only), Da Nico (Little Italy)*

<Author>nmdk226
<Content>Elevators were truly awful I stayed at the Marriott Marquis from April 9-13, 2005 for a conference. The hotel is in a wonderful location (in the heart of Times Square) and has great views of the city from the rooms and bar/lounge areas. The gym is fantastic and free. The rooms are spacious, clean and nicely decorated. But the elevators were horrible. Some mornings I had to wait 10-15 minutes for an elevator to take me down to the lower levels. What made the situation even more maddening were the big signs the hotel had posted bragging about having the most efficient elevator technology in the city. I'm shocked that the hotel hasn't done something to improve the situation, given that they must have non-stop complaints about it. Also, the recommendations that the concierge gave me for local restaurants were not very good. Despite the location, I would not stay here again. I would also recommend staying somewhere outside of Times Square if you want to be able to walk to restaurants that aren't packed with tourists and aren't a rip-off.

<Author>TJGREY
<Content>Wonderful location. And about those elevators.... This is THE place to stay if you're in town for Broadway shows, as the location cannot be beat. Hotel itself is very nice, decent-sized rooms, pretty decor. They renovated within the last two years....And yet, the elevator situation is horrible. NOT (as many previous reviews would have you believe) because of repairs, but because they are installing a computer-operated system that assigns you a car based on the floor you requested by punching a number into a keypad in the lobby or on your floor.NOBODY seemed to understand that this is how you request a car. The hotel should have instructions posted everywhere, but they don't. Which is why you get so many people stranded (the car isn't coming unless you specifically call for it).That said, there were still very few cars operating at key times because so many are being switched over to the new system. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good Location - A few things to also be aware of.... This was our first trip to NY so the Marriott Marquis proved to be a great location, right in the heart of Time Square - The hotel is extremely busy with corporate events between the ground and 8th floor and The View on the 47th floor seems to be a tourist attraction so expect long queues for the lift up there - even if your staying at the hotel! The lifts are always busy but the longest wait we had was around 5 minutes. We would recommend visiting The View Lounge for a drink to take in the skyline (takes about an hour for a full rotation) but do not recommend the restaurant - at $59 per head the food is distinctly average and not worth the money when compared to other restaurants in the same price range - the same goes for the Encore restuarant on the 8th floor - we had breakfast for 2 at $50! - there are so many restaurants/diner's in Time Square you don't need to pay that amount. The Broadway Lounge on the 8th floor is a great location to enjoy drinks/cocktails - especially if you can get a window seat overlooking Time Square. The concierge service wasn't great - we asked for advice on the best way back to JFK and was told to take a yellow cab ($60+) however, when we checked with American Express who are opposite concierge on the 8th floor they offered a shuttle service at $18 per person. On the whole we had a good stay, room was clean etc but you are definately paying for the location - we wouldn't stay here again as there are so many other hotels to try in NY.

That is the way business should be done. In this day of modern technology there is no excuse for the poor management of reservations at the Marriott. The Marriott staff kept stressing that they were going to pay for our room as if that should make everything ok, despite the potential inconvenience of being sent to a hotel 45 minutes away from where we planned to stay. As I explained to them staying at the Marriott was about convenience for the event we were planning to attend, not the price. They should not assume that everyone who stays here is only interested in getting a free room because they have poorly managed their reservation system. Saturday night we ate in the hotel restaurant on the 8th floor. Service was good and so was the food. Prices were reasonable for a tourist location. It will be hard for me to ever consider staying here again. The Marriott staff needs to be better organized. We travel very often and this is the first time in many years that we were faced with so many obstacles in such a short time. Should you be considering this hotel call to reconfirm your reservation and ask the status of their elevators. Had we had theater tickets or dinner reservations it would have been extremely difficult to arrive on time for either. I shudder to imagine what this hotel would due in the case of an emergency evacuation. There is no way they could properly handle any type of emergency.

I would recommend this hotel, it is well worth the price.

<Author>goldcardluke
<Content>Great location. Best for short trips only. The location is great. Probably the most central hotel to Times Square you can get. It's opposite the huge Virgin Megastore. I consider the hotel to be expensive, but it's worth paying the extra for a view. The price of this hotel seems to be the same at all times. There's no cheap time to stay there in my experience. On my first visit we stayed at the back of the hotel overlooking the Hudson River, but on the second visit we overlooked Times Square. It was great to sit in the comfy chairs and look out - especially at night. Though you could go down and sit in the bar and get a similar view. They have removed the mini bars from the room which is a shame. The rooms are large and comfortable. Bathrooms are good too. The lifts are a problem, but we never waited more than 5 minutes. Nice gift shop. The souvenirs were quite classy compared to the gift shops outside the hotel. The View restaurant rotates giving you views of New York. We had to queue to get in (even though we booked) but eating there was a nice treat. You have to book a couple of days in advance. We had the set menu which was quite reasonable - don't let them talk you into cocktails, champagne etc. though as this seriously bumps up the bill! The hotel is very big so there's not much of an aptmosphere, but if you're looking for comfort and convenience it's a good place to come back to at the end of a busy day. Great if you're in town for a very short visit, but you'd have to pretty well off to stay for several days.

<Author>lass=
<Content>Got the Best Room in the House--4036! My husband and I just returned from the Marriott Marquis in NYC today. I wanted to write this review while I still remembered every detail of our visit. We stayed for 4 nights and had a fabulous time. The hotel was very clean, quiet, and not any more expensive than the other hotels in the Times Square/Broadway area. If you are looking for a hotel to spend New Year's Eve in, this is the place. They have Ball Drop View Rooms available for New Year's Eve that can be booked by calling the hotel directly. I am sure they are EXPENSIVE, but this hotel by far has the best view. Actually, the ball drop is filmed for TV from this hotel! I was torn between rating this hotel as excellent or above average. We only had two problems during our stay. The first was at check in. After navigating the subway from JFK, we arrive at the check in desk only to be informed that the room we reserved was not available. Well, let me explain. It was available, but it would be $60 dollars more per night. When we reserved a room, we called the hotel directly. My husband was on business and got a special rate that was offered through the company he was coming to visit. The lady on the phone said that the rate quoted was for a city view room. Well, when we got there, ready to check in, I asked if they had any rooms overlooking Times Square. The man at the desk said, Yes. For $60 more per night. You can't have the Times Square view room for this company's rate. And, I said, o.k. then, we'll just take the city view room that is included in the rate. And, again he says, No, the Times Square view room is $60 more per night. And, I say, Well, what is a city view room? and he doesn't answer. He just stands there looking at me. Now, I know there is a difference between a city view and Times Square view room. I knew that much going into it. There are 4 different faces of the hotel, some looking in directions other than Times Square. But, obviously, this man thought they were one in the same-that city view and Times Square view were one in the same. I had just heard (via TripAdvisor) that you could ask for upgrades sometimes, especially if you were a Marriott Rewards member-which we are, and they would let you have them. The man at check in acted like I was a complete idiot for mentioning that I was a Marriott Rewards Member and said, You don't get an upgrade for that! Well, according to TripAdvisor, lots of people do. But, we must not have been one of those people. So, if you expect to be getting freebies just because you are part of the club, I wouldn't count on it. Well, the guy at the desk finally asks if this is our first time at the Marquis. When we said yes, he said, we'll I'll go ahead and let you have a Times Square View room then since it is your first time here. Well, finally......Again, I wasn't asking for the best room in the place or anything, I just wanted the city view room we had reserved. Meaning, I would like to look at SOMETHING within the confines of New York City. Considering that some on this website have said they got rooms over looking steam vents, I just wanted to make sure we got a room with an actual view. Well, the poor guy must have not understood what I meant, but my complaining paid off! When, we stepped into Room 4036, I about died! We were on the 40th floor, looking DIRECTLY at where they drop the ball for New Year's Eve. Two days before this room would have cost $1000 bucks or more! We had the best view ever and I was so glad I had a bit of a tiff with the guy, if this was my reward! We could even see the Statue of Liberty from this room, as well as Battery Park, and even a slight view of the river from the right side. A few nights, my husand and I turned the couch around to face the window and just sat and stared! Very cool! The other problem is that we were charged more for our room, by about $50 a night. Then, when we checked out, the charges had been corrected. We didn't even have to say anything. But, it did put a hold on our bank for more money than we had anticipated. I would check into how much money they are going to put on your credit card/debit card before you leave the desk. Our rate was $215, but we were charged more than the standard tax and fees. But, miraculously, it cleared itself up. We didn't bother to ask what had happened. As far as the elevators go, they were not a problem. I think people bring the elevator problems on themselves. If you expect to leave 10 minutes before your show and get there on time, you are pushing your luck. We never had a problem with the elevators, save for once, and that time it was only a 10 minute ride or less. We went up and down the elevators at various times of the day too, 7 a.m., 12 noon, 5 p.m., and all throughout the evening. The bed is nice, the couch is nice. Hated the pillows. We came back with sore necks because all the pillows were feather and go flat as soon as you lie down on them. The bathroom and room were both very spacious. The towels were some of the best hotel towels I've ever used. Very fluffy and soft. There is a fitness center, but we never used it. There is no pool, which could be disappointing to the kiddies. But, the view was fantasic and we would go back--just for the view and location of the hotel alone.

<Author>jn322jn
<Content>Great room, but that's about it. We booked a deluxe corner king room Dec. 29  30 and it was very nice. Much bigger than the average NYC room and very modern. BUT... (1) The hotel double-charged me. I used a different credit card at check-in, not the one I used to guarantee the room, then the hotel charged both cards. I must say that on New Year's Eve evening they were very helpful when I called them about it and they had one of the charges credited back to me immediately, but if the lady that checked us in had not spent most of the time on the telephone, maybe the mistake wouldn't have happened! (2) The elevators are a problem. Not as bad as some of the reviews have indicated, but it is a bothersome issue. A word to the wise...when you see room on an elevator, get in! Regardless of where the elevator might be headed, get in one when you can. And try to avoid the 8th floor. That's where check-in, shops and lounges are and as a result where most of the people are...take an escalator to a lower floor if you're on the 8th and you won't have as many people to fight with. (3) The hotel is very slow to pick up room service trays. At one point, there were three trays sitting outside of rooms on our floor and they smelled very much. We had to call to get them removed. The next day, the remains of someone's breakfast stayed in the hallway until the next morning (appx. 24 hrs.). The location of this hotel is wonderful, but you can probably do better and spend a lot less!

<Author>Manderina
<Content>If you don't have patience, don't stay at this hotel I've stayed at the Marriott Marquis twice, both for my husband's corporate functions. (Once in September 04 and again in December 04.) My one piece of advice to travelers is: don't stay at this hotel if you are inpatient! The rooms are spacious, clean, and comfortable with an amazing view, if you are lucky enough to get a Times Square view. You won't have any trouble sleeping in the comfortable beds. It truly feels like home.The revolving bar and restaurant on the top floor is a MUST see. You get a gorgeous 360 degree panoramic view of the City. However, I would never choose to stay here on a personal visit due to the elevators. They were horrible both times I stayed. It wasn't unusual to wait 20 - 45 minutes to get an elevator. (I'm not exaggerating.) We would get so excited when a door opened on our floor, but 99% of the time the elevator was completely full. People were crammed in there like sardines. Then, once you got into an elevator, it would stop on EVERY floor. Imagine being picked up on the 45th floor, the elevator is full and it stops on 44, 43, 42, you get the point. (Holding the buttons doesn't work.) It actually becomes a hilarious game, the crowd cheers when you get down more than 1 or 2 floors at a time. When the doors would open on a floor, the riders and waiters would yell back and forth to each other. At least people have a good sense of humor! If you are drunk, I highly recommend a hilarious elevator ride! In the morning, it took us an hour to get down to the lobby. There are no escalators to take you down to the lower floors. It's either wait for elevators or walk down 40 flights of stairs with your luggage.The problem is not people waiting to get a hotel view elevator. We were desperate to get on ANY elevator. I would have taken a service elevator if I could find it.The management has signs claiming that the problem will be fixed. We saw those in September, but in December it still hadn't improved. I don't know what the solution could be besides building additional elevators.If time is not an issue for you, then you'll love this hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A few words on the Marquis... The Marriott Marquis is a great hotel to stay at if it is going to be your first time in New York City. Check-in was extreamly fast. They even began to implement automatic check-in kiosks in the lobby. The elevators are another reason I gave the marriott such a low rating. There are eight elevators that service 48 floors. Unlike other hotels which have specific High rise, Low Rise, and Mid-Rise elevators, the Marriott elevators service all the floors, which means that you will spend a lot more time waiting for an elevator (Expect to wait about 10 minutes during peak times). During my stay, I found service to be extreamly slow. For example, when I asked for two extra pillows, it took housekeeping about forty-five minutes to bring them to my room! This isn't hard to understand when you figure that there are about 1886 rooms. The reason I say that you should consider this hotel if it is going to be your first time in N.Y.C. is because it is right in the center of Times Square, and Times Square is in the middle of Manhattan. At night, security in the hotel is excellent. What's remarkable about the hotel is that it caters to both businessmen and families alike. However, there are times where the hotel lobby is flooded with businessmen who are talking about the convention they just came from. All in all, if you would like excellent service, I'd find another hotel, (or the Plaza). If you want an excellent view, choose the Marriott

It seemed to cut down on the waiting and we didn't have to try and squeeze in with 25 or 30 other people!!! The elevators were a minor complaint tho...it wouldn't keep me from going back and staying there again. I would highly recommend this hotel to visitors, especially 1st time visitors to New York. Lots of variety of places to eat nearby-from the hot dog vendor to Olive Garden to McDonald's to TGI Fridays to bistros; plenty of Starbucks on almost every corner; there's the TKTS booth right down the street and after you get your discount ticket to that fabulous Broadway show, you can stroll over to visit the Naked Cowboy basically right outside your hotel...can it get any better than that??!!!LOL.....So grab a Jamba Juice and a cannolli pastry for me and enjoy your stay in, what I think, is the greatest city ever!

The only issues were that the hotel rates were too high and, as others have noted, long elevator waits. You need to exercise a good degree of patience while waiting for the elevators. They take too long to get to your floor and when they do get to your floor, they tend to be packed with people.Overall, however, it was a good experience.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice hotel I stayed from 9/17 - 9/20 with my husband staying until 9/22 for a conference. We had asked for a king sized non-smoking upper level room and was told upon arrival that only doubles existed, but that we could be moved to a different room the next day, which was fine. Went to room and found that someone had been in the room prior to our arrival -- my guess is that someone technically checked out, but didn't leave the room as the bed was messy, glasses were left out, dirty towel in the bathroom, etc. Called the front desk and we were told we would be moved to a different room. The first room had a partial view of Times Square -- the second room was on the side of the building facing behind Times Square. The situation with the rooms is the only reason I did not rate it an excellent. The next morning I received a text message advising us to dial the At Your Service number between 3 and 7 pm for our new room. At this point, my husband was not in the mood to change rooms, but I am so glad we did. We ended up on the 40th floor in room 4036 which had an incredibly spectacular room. As a NY'er visiting NYC now as a tourist, I am seeing things for the first time through new eyes and the view literally was breathtaking. Yes, the hotel elevators leave a lot to be desired, but I have been in hotels with longer wait times. All staff were cordial and polite and that is what counts. Rooms were made up daily and the room with the king sized bed had a sofa, chair and ottoman, desk, armoire with TV, closet, safe, coffee maker and coffee supplies, and nice sized bathroom. In the hotel there are restaurants and bars, but you would be crazy not to leave the hotel and venture forth into the streets to find something that suits your palate. What I really liked about the hotel is that it has not one, but two Starbucks (one on the 8th floor - small, but does the job and one on the 1st floor - regular sized), a small store with typical and not so typical tourist items for sale as well as snacks, soda, and even ice cream, but beware -- they close at 10 pm. Internet connection in your room is something like $12.95 per day and if you have a wireless card, don't expect free WiFi as you'll be notified of the $9.95 daily charge. There is a business center near the front desk, which I did not use, but was told that you could access the Internet there (not sure if that means free or not). I love the location of this hotel and if you are trying to wow friends or family or if it is your first time visiting NY, stay here. NYC is a wonderful place to visit that is safe, clean, fun and exciting. Go past all of the tourist traps and do something fun during your stay -- you'll be glad you did!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Frequent visitor-stayed again in 8/04-GREAT! Where to start? I have stayed at the Marriott Marquis many times participating at NYC conferences as an employee and as a tourist. The hotel has never failed me or my companions. This recent trip made me remember why I did not choose the Westin, The Edison or any other of the Times Square hotels nearby for a tour of NYC with my nieces.From the moment the bellman takes your bags, you are on the receiving end of top shelf service. Considering this hotel handles up to 2,000+ guests per day, I am amazed that every request is handled with smiles and total aplomb ;-). My nieces thought the bellman from Senegal was the best! Anthony? Anyway..he was their introduction to Marriott and I think they will never forget him. When we hailed a taxi later, they asked for his help specifically. A hit and a happy start for our visit. The rooms are huge by NYC standards offering very comfortable beds (fresh crisp sheets, three fluffy pillows on queen beds with leather headboards, thick foam mattresses) oversized windows with views, no noise temperature control, a desk and chair plus 2 extra chairs, multiple lighting choices, in-room entertainment systems with remote keyboards, wireless and fast access internet, granite and travertine baths with plenty of H20 force and consistent hot water, an iron, a REAL HAIRDRYER (not one of those in-wall substitutes) and thick sculted carpets and sun shielding draperies. The kids loved the remote board and the games plus new release movies.My nieces (11 and 14) had a blast riding the glass elevators and sitting at the glowing lobby sushi bar and adjacent lounge watching the massive TV outside the 8th floor windows. As a treat, I promised them room service...When we called downstairs, they asked for a special fruit plate without bananas, grapes, or strawberries. They wanted cheeses-three types to include something with blue streaks and sliced green and really red apples with bottled water, diet coke and pizza bites on bagels with extra cheese. I called with the special request and in 30 minutes, the team delivered exactly what they asked for! EXACTLY! RED apples, the blue cheeses, everything! Later, when only a latte would do, it was downstairs to the lobby for Starbucks. The only complaint about the  lounge was that it wasn't very busy, but it still took about 15 minutes for a server to approach us. Maybe the kids threw them off a bit, but we planned to have dessert there to watch the lights. The front desk staff were, as always, very pleasant. The concierge made travel arrangements for a private car post (Broadway) show as well as to the airport upon departure. She called for restaurant reservations and made appropriate recommendations for something cool for kids. The restaurant she chose was a three level mosaic inspired setting with a secret garden downstairs serving Italian food close to the theatre. Perfect. Just what we wanted.The proximity to Central Park and the shows, with easy access to Pier 83 ( a few blocks from hotel) for ferry rides and a huge marine ship tour with planes and a submarine (all hands on) couldn't be beat for the kids. A taxi to Chinatown and Little Italy will cost about $8-$10 including a tip, but subway access is very near the hotel also.The day we left, I called at 11:45 P.M. and asked that a bellman assist us around 6:25 am. At 6:19 a.m., the door knock came with a beaming and congenial helper standing outside. WOW!Check-out was a breeze through the T.V. or telephone extension and the USA Today outside my hotel door was perfect for the drive into LaGuardia.This hotel may have a f-e-w drawbacks... namely, prices (a Times Square room with a commanding view was $329-summer/weekend ), no mini-bar (for die-hards), mild waits for the elevators (during fuller capacity), BUT, there is ice and vending per floor, special discounts on rooms if you search and book early, a MARVELOUS FITNESS FACILITY and awesome staff throughout the entire hotel. When an 11 and 14 year old enter a professional work-out environment and they are greeted with we are so glad you are joining us! it almost takes your breath away. After we entered, there were 2 other parents arriving with teens and the kids were delighted to get headsets for the in-station T.V.'s and music. Not one person raised an eyebrow.Finally, for the team that never gets enough credit, maintenance and housekeeping are to be commended. The hotel is clean, the rooms are spotless, the water pressure good, security is alert and ready to help you upon request. Every morning, when we left the room, the housekeeper smiled at the kids and asked about their exciting yesterday. Yes, I am biased. If there is any competition to this hotel in Times Square, I'll try it. But for now, I remain an MM fan.Go Marriott Marquis! You are worth every penny, every time!Bridget RigdonAtlanta. Georgia

<Author>seetheworld25
<Content>Good Location, Not Worth Your Money We stayed at the Marquis in March, 2004. We were amazed at the great location of the hotel- we walked out and we were on Times Square. Plus we got there and there were no standard rooms left, so they upgraded us for free to a Times Square view. But overall, the hotel is not worth your money. You are paying for the location and that's pretty much it. The rooms are nothing special, they're just average, standard sized rooms. We were on the 42nd floor, but we could still hear the street sounds which was annoying when we were trying to fall asleep. The elevators take forever to get, so plan on allowing 15-20 minutes extra just to catch one. The staff was very unhelpful and not incredibly friendly. We asked the concierge about how to get to Ground Zero and it took her 20 minutes to first of all find the map and then figure out herself how to explain to us how to get there. You'd think that was a pretty common question! But it did have a great fitness room with floor to ceiling windows overlooking Times Square and it had a great restaurant/lounge at the top of the hotel that overlooked all of New York's skyline. I would probably stay there again if I got a good deal, but I definately would not pay $300 a night again.

<Author>tombstonemarshal
<Content>Near Perfection! We had the distinct pleasure of staying at the Marriott Marquis last month. What a wonderful hotel! It's a big, hustle-bustle hotel, a microcosm of the city itself. The room we stayed in was large, immaculate, and comfortable. We looked out directly on Times Square, the crossroads of the world. The staff is energetic, attentive, and professional. What more could you ask? The location is superb. One can walk everywhere, and indeed we did enjoy walks to Central Park, Fifth Avenue and Union Square. We experienced none of the famous elevator problems that other Tripadvisor reviewers have noted, although we were at the hotel on what appeared to be a fairly slow weekend for New York. To the extent a $200 a night hotel room can ever be a bargain, the Marriott Marquis certainly qualifies.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Best Location in New York! Great Hotel! My friend and I just returned from our 2nd stay at the Marriott Marquis (3 nights - Thurs March 25th thru Sunday March 28th). We also stayed there in 2003 for 3 nights in February. I love this hotel. It is close to everything in Times Square - especially for theater going. I've been very happy with the service and have had no problems. Staff is friendly and courteous. The hotel has good security and is in a safe location. Both rooms have been very large for New York City and have had great views (one faced South and one faced North). The room we stayed in this year was on the 42nd floor. It was not yet rennovated, but was nice nonetheless. The rennovators were up to the 36th  37th floors (all the floors below are completed). I snuck a peak at a rennovated room and thought they were nicely decorated and the bathrooms are much more attractive. All rennovations should be completed by mid-summer 2004. Our rate was $239 a night, which was about average for the nicer Times Square area hotels. This stay was during peak Spring-Break time, too.  We had no trouble checking in. We arrived around 12:30pm on a Thursday, so we were early for the standard check-in time of 3pm. Our room wasn't yet ready, so we checked our bags and went to lunch at Roxy's Deli next door. We came back at 2pm and our room was ready. Throughout our stay, I could see that there are definitely busier times for checking in where wait times could be long. Checkout is easy using the phone or TV. We requested a late checkout on Sunday (1pm instead of Noon). We checked out bags again and came back around 5pm to pick them up. No problems or delays.  The elevators are fast. During peak times, there can be a 5-10 minute wait to get one, but most times, we waited 2-3 minutes max. We also had no trouble using the high-speed Internet connection (which is $12.95 a day).  I have reservations to go back to the Marriott Marquis in late May 2004 with my mom. Last time I took her to NYC in early 2001, we stayed at a small hotel on 58th street near Columbus Circle. It had tiny rooms with tiny twin beds (about 18 apart and one pressed against the wall), a crampt little bathroom with a pedestal sink with no counter space, and a small window with no view but the wall of the building next door a few feet away. All that for the bargain price of $179 a nite! I'll never take my chances again on an unknown hotel again.  I highly recommend the Marriott Marquis.

If you have plans, just leave a couple of minutes early to keep yourself on schedule! You should have no problems if you leave early! Just check when you check in for the fire escapes if you are nervous about the elevators or if you find yourself in a case of an emergency! But if you stay here, I promise that you'll enjoy it! Oh, the peanuts that you can get in the bar on the 8th floor are GOOD! Try some! I am going back in early April 2004, and unfortunately I have to stay somewhere else! :( I Hope you stay here, you won't regret it! I had a wonderful time at the Marriott Marquis New York! :)

<Content>Cracking, absolutely cracking...! When you're on a cheapo rate you generally expect a view of the air conditioning plant or, if you're really lucky, the back of the kitchen, but in this case, they did not lie! I walked in through the door into a newly refurbished room which had no end wall, just a window - and the view was amazing, all of the south end of Times Square - including loads of flashing billboards and the Good Morning America studio!The lifts (elevators), yep, they're a problem, but only that you have to allow yourself a bit more time in the morning and evening and be prepared to get intimate with everyone in the lift (some would say that's nothing to worry about!!) but once the refurbishment's done, they're going to be the best elevators in New York (is that really a selling point?! As long as they're fast, that's all that matters!)The room was really clean, comfy beds, good room service - bath's one of those small low shower tray/bath things, that's about the only (very small) gripe.View through the atrium is amazing - I was on the 17th floor and really enjoyed people watching in the bars and restaurants below - like little ants moving about it's so high!All in all, 10/10 - a superb hotel now they're refurbishing it, and the lifts are just a minor problem at the moment - don't let them stop you from staying.
